## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-camel-arch-001: Apache Camel Message Routing Architecture

## Task

Trace how Apache Camel routes a message from endpoint reception through the EIP pipeline to a destination. Map the complete Component→Endpoint→Consumer→Processor→Producer hierarchy, including the Pipeline processor chain, Channel interceptor wiring, and the RouteReifier model-to-runtime bridge.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/camel--1006f047 (mirror of apache/camel) (Java, ~2.8M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: core/ — the Camel core routing engine (camel-api, camel-support, camel-core-processor, camel-base-engine, camel-core-reifier)

## Requirements

1. Identify all relevant components in the Component→Endpoint→Consumer→Processor→Producer hierarchy (API interfaces + base implementations)
2. Trace the dependency chain from route definition through reification to runtime message processing
3. Document the Pipeline and Channel architecture (how processors are chained and intercepted)
4. Explain how the RouteReifier bridges the DSL model (RouteDefinition) to the runtime Route

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

322026-03-08T19:13:41.631051agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the Apache Camel message routing architecture. Let me synthesize what I've found:

## Architecture Overview

### 1. API Interfaces (camel-api)
- **Component** (`org.apache.camel.Component`) - Factory for Endpoints; `createEndpoint(String uri)` is the key method
- **Endpoint** (`org.apache.camel.Endpoint`) - Message Endpoint pattern; creates Consumers and Producers; `createConsumer(Processor)`, `createProducer()`, `createAsyncProducer()`
- **Consumer** (`org.apache.camel.Consumer`) - Consumes messages from an Endpoint; holds a `Processor` reference; `createExchange(boolean autoRelease)`
- **Processor** (`org.apache.camel.Processor`) - Core functional interface; `void process(Exchange exchange)`
- **Producer** (`org.apache.camel.Producer`) - extends Processor, Service, IsSingleton, EndpointAware; sends messages to an Endpoint
- **Channel** (`org.apache.camel.Channel`) - extends AsyncProcessor, Navigate<Processor>; sits between Processors in the route graph; `initChannel(...)`, `postInitChannel()`, `getOutput()`, `getNextProcessor()`
- **Route** (`org.apache.camel.Route`) - Runtime route object

### 2. Base Implementations (camel-support)
- **DefaultComponent** (`org.apache.camel.support.DefaultComponent`) - Abstract base for all components; extends ServiceSupport, implements Component
- **DefaultEndpoint** (`org.apache.camel.support.DefaultEndpoint`) - Abstract base for endpoints
- **DefaultConsumer** (`org.apache.camel.support.DefaultConsumer`) - Base consumer; holds endpoint + processor; creates exchanges via ExchangeFactory; `defaultConsumerCallback()` returns AsyncCallback
- **DefaultProducer** (`org.apache.camel.support.DefaultProducer`) - Base producer

### 3. Runtime Engine (camel-base-engine)

362026-03-08T19:15:54.037457agentmessage-
The analysis is complete. Here's a summary of what I found and documented:

## Apache Camel Message Routing Architecture — Key Findings

### Component→Endpoint→Consumer→Processor→Producer Hierarchy

The hierarchy is cleanly separated across API interfaces in `camel-api` with base implementations in `camel-support`:

- **`Component`** — URI-scheme-based factory for `Endpoint` objects (`createEndpoint(String uri)`)
- **`Endpoint`** — Creates `Consumer` (inbound) and `Producer` (outbound); also creates `Exchange` objects
- **`Consumer`** (`DefaultConsumer`) — Receives transport messages, creates `Exchange` via `ExchangeFactory`, invokes the route processor chain
- **`Processor`** — Core `@FunctionalInterface` with `void process(Exchange)`
- **`Producer`** — Extends `Processor`; sends exchanges to a destination endpoint

### Pipeline and Channel Architecture

- **`Pipeline`** (`camel-core-processor`) — Implements Pipes and Filters EIP; uses an inner `PipelineTask` with `ReactiveExecutor` for non-blocking async processing; calls `ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn()` between steps
- **`RoutePipeline`** — Marker subclass of `Pipeline` used as the top-level route pipeline
- **`DefaultChannel`** (`camel-base-engine`) — Extends `CamelInternalProcessor`, implements `Channel`; sits between every processor node; `initChannel()` applies `InterceptStrategy` decorators (in reverse priority order), tracing, debugging, and message history advices; `setErrorHandler()` wraps the chain in error handling; `postInitChannel()` adds JMX instrumentation

### RouteReifier Model-to-Runtime Bridge

`RouteReifier.doCreateRoute()` is the central bridge:
1. Resolves the input `Endpoint` from `RouteDefinition.getInput()`
2. Creates a `DefaultRoute` via `RouteFactory`
3. For each output `ProcessorDefinition
... (truncated)

  "thought": "Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the Apache Camel message routing architecture. Let me synthesize what I've found:\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\n### 1. API Interfaces (camel-api)\n- **Component** (`org.apache.camel.Component`) - Factory for Endpoints; `createEndpoint(String uri)` is the key method\n- **Endpoint** (`org.apache.camel.Endpoint`) - Message Endpoint pattern; creates Consumers and Producers; `createConsumer(Processor)`, `createProducer()`, `createAsyncProducer()`\n- **Consumer** (`org.apache.camel.Consumer`) - Consumes messages from an Endpoint; holds a `Processor` reference; `createExchange(boolean autoRelease)`\n- **Processor** (`org.apache.camel.Processor`) - Core functional interface; `void process(Exchange exchange)`\n- **Producer** (`org.apache.camel.Producer`) - extends Processor, Service, IsSingleton, EndpointAware; sends messages to an Endpoint\n- **Channel** (`org.apache.camel.Channel`) - extends AsyncProcessor, Navigate<Processor>; sits between Processors in the route graph; `initChannel(...)`, `postInitChannel()`, `getOutput()`, `getNextProcessor()`\n- **Route** (`org.apache.camel.Route`) - Runtime route object\n\n### 2. Base Implementations (camel-support)\n- **DefaultComponent** (`org.apache.camel.support.DefaultComponent`) - Abstract base for all components; extends ServiceSupport, implements Component\n- **DefaultEndpoint** (`org.apache.camel.support.DefaultEndpoint`) - Abstract base for endpoints\n- **DefaultConsumer** (`org.apache.camel.support.DefaultConsumer`) - Base consumer; holds endpoint + processor; creates exchanges via ExchangeFactory; `defaultConsumerCallback()` returns AsyncCallback\n- **DefaultProducer** (`org.apache.camel.support.DefaultProducer`) - Base producer\n\n### 3. Runtime Engine (camel-base-engine)\n- **DefaultChannel** (`org.apache.camel.impl.engine.DefaultChannel`) - extends CamelInternalProcessor, implements Channel; the key interceptor/error-handler wiring point; `initChannel()` adds advices (tracing, debugging, message history, interceptors); `postInitChannel()` adds JMX instrumentation; `getOutput()` returns errorHandler if set, else output\n- **DefaultRoute** (`org.apache.camel.impl.engine.DefaultRoute`) - implements Route; holds `eventDrivenProcessors` list, `interceptStrategies`, consumer, endpoint\n\n### 4. Processors (camel-core-processor)\n- **Pipeline** (`org.apache.camel.processor.Pipeline`) - Implements the Pipes and Filters EIP; holds a list of AsyncProcessors; uses PipelineTask (inner class) with ReactiveExecutor for async processing; `process(Exchange, AsyncCallback)` schedules PipelineTask; PipelineTask.run() iterates through processors calling `processor.process(exchange, this)` and uses `ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn()` between steps\n- **RoutePipeline** (`org.apache.camel.processor.RoutePipeline`) - extends Pipeline; used as the top-level pipeline for a Route\n- **SendProcessor** (`org.apache.camel.processor.SendProcessor`) - Forwards exchanges to a static endpoint destination; holds an AsyncProducer; uses ProducerCache\n\n### 5. Reifier Layer (camel-core-reifier)\n- **ProcessorReifier** (`org.apache.camel.reifier.ProcessorReifier`) - Abstract base; `reifier(Route, ProcessorDefinition)` factory method maps definition types to reifier instances; `addRoutes()` calls `makeProcessor()` \u2192 `Channel` \u2192 adds to `route.getEventDrivenProcessors()`; `wrapChannel()` creates a DefaultChannel, adds interceptors, wraps in error handler; `createOutputsProcessor()` creates child processors and wraps each in a Channel; `createCompositeProcessor()` creates a Pipeline\n- **RouteReifier** (`org.apache.camel.reifier.RouteReifier`) - extends ProcessorReifier<RouteDefinition>; `createRoute()` \u2192 `doCreateRoute()`:\n  1. Resolves the input Endpoint from RouteDefinition\n  2. Creates a Route via RouteFactory\n  3. Configures route properties (tracing, message history, stream caching, etc.)\n  4. Iterates over output ProcessorDefinitions, calling `ProcessorReifier.reifier(route, output).addRoutes()` for each\n  5. Collects `eventDrivenProcessors` from the route\n  6. Creates a `RoutePipeline` wrapping all event-driven processors\n  7. Wraps RoutePipeline in `InternalProcessor` (adds UnitOfWork, route policy, inflight tracking, JMX, lifecycle advices)\n  8. Sets the InternalProcessor as `route.setProcessor(internal)`\n- **PipelineReifier** (`org.apache.camel.reifier.PipelineReifier`) - calls `createChildProcessor(true)` which calls `createOutputsProcessor()` \u2192 creates Pipeline\n\n### 6. Model (camel-core-model)\n- **RouteDefinition** - DSL model for a route; has `input` (from endpoint) and `outputs` (list of ProcessorDefinitions)\n- **ProcessorDefinition** - Base for all EIP definitions\n\n## Complete Message Flow\n\n### Build/Startup Phase (Model \u2192 Runtime):\n1. User defines route using DSL \u2192 creates `RouteDefinition` with `ProcessorDefinition` outputs\n2. `RouteReifier.createRoute()` is called (triggered by `AbstractCamelContext` during startup)\n3. For each output `ProcessorDefinition`, `ProcessorReifier.reifier(route, output)` creates the appropriate reifier\n4. Each reifier's `addRoutes()` calls `makeProcessor()` which calls `createProcessor()` (abstract, implemented by each reifier) then `wrapProcessor()` \u2192 `wrapChannel()`\n5. `wrapChannel()` creates a `DefaultChannel`, calls `channel.initChannel()` (adds tracing/debugging/interceptor advices), optionally wraps in error handler, calls `channel.postInitChannel()` (adds JMX instrumentation)\n6. The Channel is added to `route.getEventDrivenProcessors()`\n7. After all outputs processed, `RouteReifier` creates `RoutePipeline(eventDrivenProcessors)` \n8. `RoutePipeline` is wrapped in `CamelInternalProcessor` (adds UoW, route policy, inflight, JMX, lifecycle advices)\n9. `route.setProcessor(internal)` - the InternalProcessor becomes the route's main processor\n10. The input Endpoint creates a Consumer with this processor: `endpoint.createConsumer(internal)`\n\n### Runtime Message Processing:\n1. Consumer receives a message from the transport layer\n2. Consumer creates an Exchange via `exchangeFactory.create(endpoint, autoRelease)`\n3. Consumer calls `asyncProcessor.process(exchange, callback)` where asyncProcessor is the CamelInternalProcessor\n4. CamelInternalProcessor runs its advices (UoW setup, route policy, inflight tracking, etc.) then delegates to RoutePipeline\n5. RoutePipeline.PipelineTask iterates through the list of Channel processors\n6. Each Channel (DefaultChannel) runs its advices (tracing, debugging, message history, interceptors) then delegates to the actual Processor (e.g., SetBodyProcessor, SendProcessor, etc.)\n7. For `to(\"endpoint\")` steps: SendProcessor uses ProducerCache to get/create an AsyncProducer, calls `producer.process(exchange, callback)` which sends to the destination Endpoint\n8. Between pipeline steps, `ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn()` copies OUT message to IN for the next step\n9. When all steps complete, the callback chain unwinds back to the Consumer's DefaultConsumerCallback\n10. DefaultConsumerCallback handles exceptions and releases the exchange\n\n## Key Design Patterns:\n1. **Pipes and Filters** - Pipeline processor chains processors sequentially\n2. **Message Endpoint** - Component/Endpoint/Consumer/Producer hierarchy\n3. **Decorator/Chain of Responsibility** - Channel wraps processors with interceptors and error handlers\n4. **Factory Method** - Component.createEndpoint(), Endpoint.createConsumer()/createProducer()\n5. **Template Method** - ProcessorReifier.addRoutes() calls abstract createProcessor()\n6. **Visitor/Strategy** - InterceptStrategy.wrapProcessorInInterceptors()\n7. **Advice** - CamelInternalProcessorAdvice for cross-cutting concerns\n8. **Reactive/Async** - ReactiveExecutor schedules PipelineTask for non-blocking processing\n"

Applies `InterceptStrategy.wrapProcessorInInterceptors()` for each interceptor (in reverse order), building a decorator chain around `nextProcessor`; result stored as `output`\n   - Optionally wraps `channel.getOutput()` in an error handler via `wrapChannelInErrorHandler()` \u2192 `channel.setErrorHandler(errorHandler)`\n   - Calls `channel.postInitChannel()` to add JMX instrumentation advice\n   - Returns the fully initialized `Channel`\n\n6. **Adds to route**: `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultRoute.java` (`getEventDrivenProcessors().add(channel)`)  \n   Each `Channel` is added to the route's `eventDrivenProcessors` list.\n\n7. **Assembles**: `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/RoutePipeline.java` (in `RouteReifier.doCreateRoute()`)  \n   After all outputs are processed, `RouteReifier` creates `new RoutePipeline(camelContext, eventDrivenProcessors)` \u2014 a `Pipeline` subclass that sequences all the `Channel` processors.\n\n8. **Wraps**: `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/CamelInternalProcessor.java` (via `InternalProcessorFactory.addUnitOfWorkProcessorAdvice()`)  \n   The `RoutePipeline` is wrapped in a `CamelInternalProcessor` that adds:\n   - `UnitOfWorkProcessorAdvice` (transaction boundary)\n   - `RoutePolicyAdvice` (route lifecycle hooks)\n   - `RouteInflightRepositoryAdvice` (inflight exchange tracking)\n   - `ManagementInterceptStrategy` (JMX performance stats)\n   - `RouteLifecycleAdvice` (start/stop events)\n   - Optional: `RestBindingAdvice`, `ContractAdvice`, `VariableAdvice`\n\n9. **Sets processor**: `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultRoute.java` (`route.setProcessor(internal)`)  \n   The `CamelInternalProcessor` becomes the route's main processor.\n\n10. **Creates consumer**: `core/camel-api/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/Endpoint.java` (`endpoint.createConsumer(internal)`)  \n    The input `Endpoint` creates a `Consumer` with the `CamelInternalProcessor` as its processor. The consumer is started by `RouteService`.\n\n### Runtime Message Processing Phase\n\n11. **Message arrives**: `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultConsumer.java`  \n    The transport-specific consumer (e.g., JMS, HTTP, Timer) receives a message and calls `createExchange(autoRelease)` \u2192 `exchangeFactory.create(endpoint, autoRelease)` to create an `Exchange`.\n\n12. **Dispatches**: `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultConsumer.java` (`asyncProcessor.process(exchange, callback)`)  \n    The consumer calls `process()` on its `asyncProcessor` (the `CamelInternalProcessor`), passing a `DefaultConsumerCallback` as the completion callback.\n\n13. **Runs advices**: `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/CamelInternalProcessor.java`  \n    Executes all registered `CamelInternalProcessorAdvice` instances (UoW setup, route policy `onExchangeBegin`, inflight increment, etc.) then delegates to the `RoutePipeline`.\n\n14. **Sequences processors**: `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/Pipeline.java` (via `RoutePipeline`)  \n    `Pipeline.process(exchange, callback)` acquires a `PipelineTask` from the `taskFactory` and schedules it via `ReactiveExecutor.scheduleMain(task)`. `PipelineTask.run()` iterates through the `Channel` list:\n    - Checks `exchange.isRouteStop()` and `PipelineHelper.continueProcessing()` (exception/stop checks)\n    - Calls `ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn(exchange)` to propagate the OUT message as the next IN\n    - Calls `processors.get(index++).process(exchange, this)` on the next `Channel`\n    - When all processors are done, calls `ExchangeHelper.copyResults()` and schedules the original callback\n\n15. **Applies cross-cutting concerns**: `core/camel-base-engine/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/impl/engine/DefaultChannel.java`  \n    Each `Channel` (a `CamelInternalProcessor`) runs its own advice chain (tracing, message history, interceptors) then delegates to `getOutput()` \u2014 which is either the `errorHandler` (wrapping the actual processor) or the interceptor-wrapped processor directly.\n\n16. **Executes EIP processor**: e.g., `core/camel-core-processor/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/processor/SendProcessor.java`  \n    For `to(\"endpoint\")` steps, `SendProcessor.process(exchange, callback)` uses `ProducerCache` to obtain an `AsyncProducer` for the destination `Endpoint`, then calls `producer.process(exchange, callback)` to send the message.\n\n17. **Completes**: `core/camel-support/src/main/java/org/apache/camel/support/DefaultConsumer.java` (`DefaultConsumerCallback.done()`)  \n    When the pipeline completes, the callback chain unwinds to `DefaultConsumerCallback.done()`, which handles any unhandled exceptions via `ExceptionHandler` and releases the exchange back to the `ExchangeFactory`.\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n**1. Pipes and Filters (EIP)**  \n`Pipeline` is the canonical implementation. It holds an ordered list of `AsyncProcessor` instances and sequences them, passing the output of each step as the input to the next via `ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn()`. `RoutePipeline` is a marker subclass used as the top-level pipeline for a route, distinguishing it from nested pipelines created by `PipelineDefinition`.\n\n**2. Message Endpoint (EIP)**  \nThe `Component \u2192 Endpoint \u2192 Consumer/Producer` hierarchy directly implements the Message Endpoint pattern. `Component` is a factory for `Endpoint` objects (resolved by URI scheme). `Endpoint` is a factory for `Consumer` (inbound) and `Producer` (outbound). This cleanly separates transport concerns from routing logic.\n\n**3. Decorator / Chain of Responsibility**  \n`DefaultChannel` is the central decorator. During `initChannel()`, it applies `InterceptStrategy` instances in reverse-priority order, each wrapping the previous processor via `strategy.wrapProcessorInInterceptors()`. The result is a nested decorator chain: `interceptorN \u2192 ... \u2192 interceptor1 \u2192 actualProcessor`. The error handler is then placed around this entire chain. `CamelInternalProcessor` uses a similar advice pattern at the route level.\n\n**4. Template Method**  \n`ProcessorReifier` defines the skeleton algorithm in `addRoutes()` (call `makeProcessor()`, wrap in `Channel`, add to route). Concrete reifier subclasses (e.g., `PipelineReifier`, `SendReifier`, `ChoiceReifier`) implement the abstract `createProcessor()` method to produce the specific runtime `Processor`.\n\n**5. Factory Method**  \n`ProcessorReifier.reifier(Route, ProcessorDefinition)` is a static factory that maps each `ProcessorDefinition` subtype to its corresponding `ProcessorReifier` subtype via a large `instanceof` chain (with a pluggable `PROCESSORS` map for custom reifiers). Similarly, `Component.createEndpoint()` and `Endpoint.createConsumer()/createProducer()` are factory methods.\n\n**6. Advice / AOP**  \n`CamelInternalProcessor` implements an advice pattern: it holds a list of `CamelInternalProcessorAdvice<T>` objects, each with `before(exchange)` and `after(exchange, data)` methods. This allows cross-cutting concerns (UoW, tracing, message history, JMX, route policy) to be applied uniformly without modifying the core processor logic.\n\n**7. Reactive/Async Processing**  \n`Pipeline` uses `ReactiveExecutor` to schedule `PipelineTask` objects. `PipelineTask` implements both `PooledExchangeTask` and `AsyncCallback`, allowing it to serve as its own continuation. When a processor completes asynchronously, it calls `done(false)` on the task, which re-schedules itself via `reactiveExecutor.schedule(this)` to process the next step. This enables non-blocking, event-driven routing without thread-per-exchange overhead.\n\n**8. Object Pool**  \n`ExchangeFactory` and `PooledTaskFactory` implement object pooling for `Exchange` and `PipelineTask` objects respectively, reducing GC pressure in high-throughput scenarios.\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility |\n|-----------|---------------|\n| `Component` | URI-scheme-based factory for `Endpoint` objects; manages component-level configuration |\n| `Endpoint` | Represents a communication channel; factory for `Consumer` and `Producer`; creates `Exchange` objects |\n| `Consumer` | Transport-specific message receiver; creates `Exchange`, invokes the route processor, manages `UnitOfWork` |\n| `Processor` | Core processing unit; transforms/routes an `Exchange` |\n| `Producer` | Transport-specific message sender; sends an `Exchange` to a destination `Endpoint` |\n| `Channel` (DefaultChannel) | Inter-processor conduit; applies interceptors, tracing, debugging, message history, and error handling around each processor node |\n| `Pipeline` / `RoutePipeline` | Sequences a list of processors; manages async continuation via `PipelineTask` and `ReactiveExecutor` |\n| `CamelInternalProcessor` | Route-level advice container; applies UoW, route policy, inflight tracking, JMX, and lifecycle advices |\n| `ProcessorReifier` | Model-to-runtime bridge for individual EIP nodes; creates processors and wraps them in Channels |\n| `RouteReifier` | Model-to-runtime bridge for entire routes; orchestrates the full reification pipeline |\n| `RouteDefinition` | DSL model (design-time); carries the route's structural definition |\n| `DefaultRoute` | Runtime route object; holds the assembled processor graph, consumer, and route metadata |\n\n### Data Flow Description\n\n**Design Time (DSL \u2192 Model):**  \nUser writes `from(\"timer:tick\").setBody().constant(\"hello\").to(\"log:out\")` \u2192 Java DSL fluent builders create a `RouteDefinition` with `input = TimerEndpoint URI` and `outputs = [SetBodyDefinition, ToDefinition]`.\n\n**Startup (Model \u2192 Runtime):**  \n`AbstractCamelContext.start()` \u2192 `RouteReifier.createRoute()` \u2192 for each output definition, `ProcessorReifier.reifier(route, def).addRoutes()` \u2192 `createProcessor()` (e.g., `SetBodyProcessor`, `SendProcessor`) \u2192 `wrapChannel()` \u2192 `DefaultChannel.initChannel()` (applies interceptors/advices) \u2192 `DefaultChannel.setErrorHandler()` \u2192 `DefaultChannel.postInitChannel()` \u2192 Channel added to `route.eventDrivenProcessors` \u2192 `RoutePipeline(eventDrivenProcessors)` \u2192 `CamelInternalProcessor(RoutePipeline)` \u2192 `route.setProcessor(internal)` \u2192 `endpoint.createConsumer(internal)` \u2192 consumer started.\n\n**Runtime (Message Processing):**  \nExternal message arrives \u2192 `DefaultConsumer.createExchange()` \u2192 `asyncProcessor.process(exchange, DefaultConsumerCallback)` \u2192 `CamelInternalProcessor` runs route-level advices \u2192 `RoutePipeline.process()` \u2192 `ReactiveExecutor.scheduleMain(PipelineTask)` \u2192 `PipelineTask.run()` iterates Channels \u2192 each `DefaultChannel` runs node-level advices \u2192 delegates to actual `Processor` (e.g., `SetBodyProcessor.process()` mutates exchange body; `SendProcessor.process()` obtains `AsyncProducer` from `ProducerCache` and calls `producer.process()`) \u2192 `ExchangeHelper.prepareOutToIn()` between steps \u2192 pipeline completes \u2192 `DefaultConsumerCallback.done()` \u2192 exception handling \u2192 exchange released to pool.\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n- **Component \u2192 Endpoint**: `Component.createEndpoint(String uri)` returns a configured `Endpoint`; the URI scheme determines which `Component` is used (resolved by `CamelContext.getComponent(scheme)`)\n- **Endpoint \u2192 Consumer**: `Endpoint.createConsumer(Processor processor)` \u2014 the `Processor` passed is the fully assembled route processor (CamelInternalProcessor); the Consumer is responsible for creating Exchanges and invoking this processor\n- **Endpoint \u2192 Producer**: `Endpoint.createProducer()` \u2014 returns a `Producer` that can send exchanges to the endpoint's transport\n- **Consumer \u2192 Processor**: `Consumer.getProcessor()` returns the route's entry processor; the consumer calls `processor.process(exchange)` or `asyncProcessor.process(exchange, callback)`\n- **Channel \u2192 Processor**: `Channel.getNextProcessor()` returns the unwrapped actual processor; `Channel.getOutput()` returns the fully decorated processor (with interceptors and error handler)\n- **ProcessorReifier \u2192 Channel**: `wrapChannel(processor, child)` creates a `DefaultChannel`, initializes it with the processor and interceptors, and returns it\n- **RouteReifier \u2192 Route**: `doCreateRoute()` populates `route.eventDrivenProcessors`, sets `route.processor`, and returns the `Route` object\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nApache Camel routes messages through a layered architecture built around the **Component \u2192 Endpoint \u2192 Consumer \u2192 Processor \u2192 Producer** hierarchy: a `Component` (factory) creates `Endpoint` objects from URIs; each `Endpoint` creates a `Consumer` (inbound) that receives messages and invokes the route's processor chain, or a `Producer` (outbound) that sends messages to a destination. The **RouteReifier** bridges the DSL model (`RouteDefinition` with its `ProcessorDefinition` outputs) to the runtime by iterating each output node, delegating to the appropriate `ProcessorReifier` subclass to create the concrete `Processor`, and wrapping each in a `DefaultChannel` that applies interceptors, tracing, debugging, and error handling as a decorator chain. The assembled `Channel` list is sequenced by a `RoutePipeline` (a `Pipeline` subclass) which uses a `ReactiveExecutor`-scheduled `PipelineTask` for non-blocking async processing, and the entire pipeline is wrapped in a `CamelInternalProcessor` that applies route-level cross-cutting concerns (UnitOfWork, route policy, JMX, inflight tracking) before the consumer starts receiving messages.\n",
